772	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">  Aa. Na. Ma. Selim Ullah. Vs.  Kamrun Nahar Kamal, (Ahmed Sohel, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 3929 of 2014  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J And Ahmed Sohel, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Saifuddin Chowdhury, Advocate  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Aa. Na. Ma. Selim Ullah </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Kamrun Nahar Kamal and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 199px;" width="538"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 237.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ahmed Sohel, J. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__C.%20R.%203929%20of%2014_Ahmed%20Sohel,%20J.__4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 214.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Aa. Na. Ma. Selim Ullah</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Defendant-Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Kamrun Nahar Kamal and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Plaintiff-Opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Order VII, Rule 11</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">To decide the fate of a plaint under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, averments in the plaint have to be read without looking at the defense and as such whether the registered deed of partition is a sale deed or a decree of Court or a family settlement deed among the co-sharers for their ancestral properties and registration and endorsement was genuine, regular and in order and plaintiffs have no possession over the suit land rather the petitioner is in possession of the same, in our view all these issues can only be decided by taking evidence by the trial Court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                             </span>. . .(31 and 36)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Order VII, Rule 11</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It appears that the grounds urged for in the application for rejection of plaint are absolutely the subject matter of evidence, which cannot be decided before taking evidence.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . . (34)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ismat Zerin Khan Vs. The World Bank and others 11 MLR (AD) 58;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Bangladesh Jatiya Samabaya Shilpa Samity Ltd. Vs. M/S Shan Hosiery, Proprietor Md. Abu Taleb and others, 12 BLT (AD) 253;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Abdul Malek Sawdagar Vs. Md. Mahbubey Alam, 57 DLR (AD)18, Nur Muhammad Vs. Mainuddin, 39DLR (AD) 1; Abul Khair (Md) Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd., 53 DLR (AD) 62, Bangladesh Shilpa Rin Sangstha Vs. Rahman Textile Mills Ltd., 51 DLR (AD) 221, Nurunnessa Vs. Mohiuddin Chowdhury 49 DLR (AD) 234, Eastern Bank Ltd Vs. Sub-Ordinate Judge, 49 DLR 531, Anath Bandhu Guha &amp; Sons Ltd. Through its Attorney Md. Sirajul Hoq Vs. Babu Sudhangshu Shekhar Halder, 42 DLR (AD) 244, Kazi (Md) Shahajahan and another Vs. Md. Khalilur Rahman Madbar and others, 54 DLR (AD) 125;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">M/S Crescent Petroleum Ltd Vs. Manchegorsk and another AIR 2000 Bom 161 at 168 and</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Jalil and others Vs. Islamic Bank Bangladesh Limited and others 53 DLR (AD) 12 ref</span>.</em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. Saifuddin Chowdhury, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. M. Sadequr Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">. . . For the opposite party Nos.1-6</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Ahmed Sohel, J:</span></u></strong><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">This Rule was issued calling upon the opposite party Nos. 1-6 to show cause as to why the impugned Order dated 27.03.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Chattogram in Other Suit No.09 of 2011 rejecting an application for rejection of the plaint should not be set-aside.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Relevant facts for disposal of the Rule, in short, are that the predecessor of the opposite parties No.1-5 and opposite party No.6 herein on 10.01.2011, as plaintiffs filed Other Suit No.09 of 2011 before the Court of Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Chattogram for declaration and cancellation of partition deed No.2990 dated 01.03.2009 executed and registered between them with some auxiliary relief on the contentions amongst others that the parties of the instant suit being legal heirs of deceased Wahidul Hoque and the plaintiffs and others agreed to relinquish their respective shares in favour of other co-sharers. The Relinquish/Release was part of compromise upon family settlement vide registered deed of partition No.2990 dated 01.03.2009 and also all the parties of the suit were benefited by the transaction made between them.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">During pendency of the suit the defendant No.3 filed an application on 16.06.2011 under Order VII Rule 11 read with Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure, praying for rejecting the plaint of Other Suit No.09 of 2011 on the grounds amongst others that the suit has been filed without cause of action and the suit is also barred by law.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The plaintiffs contested the said application filed under Order VII Rule 11 read with section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure of the defendant No.3, by filing a written objection denying all the material allegations made in the said application. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The defendant No.12 submitted a written statement by denying the averments made in the plaint and supporting the family settlement of their ancestral properties vide registered deed of partition No.2990 dated 01.03.2009. In the said written statement, she asserts that the plaintiffs have no right “Lawful exercise and others prevent of right of this defendant” and she prayed for dismissing the suit with cost.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The predecessor of the opposite party Nos.1-5 and opposite party No.6 instituted the instant suit for cancellation of the partition deed No.2990 dated 01.03.2009 as they are the party/executants of the same but the petitioner Nos.1-5 substituted as 1(Ka)-1(Uma) vide Order No.17 dated 14.03.2013 as the legal heirs of deceased plaintiff No.1 and on this point only the suit for cancellation of deed is not maintainable in the eye of law.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">After hearing both the parties, the learned</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;"> Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Chattogram passed the impugned Order dated 27.03.2014 in Other Suit No.9 of 2011 and thereby rejected the application filed under Order VII Rule 11 read with Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned Order dated 27.03.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Chattogram in Other Suit No.09 of 2011, the present defendant-petitioner filed this revisional application before this Court under Section 115 (1) of the Code of Civil Procedure and obtained the present Rule and stay.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. Saifuddin Ahmed Chowdhury, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner supports the Rule and submits that the learned Judge of the trial Court erred in law in rejecting the application for rejection of plaint without applying its judicious mind to the facts and circumstances of the case and thereby committed an error of law occasioning failure of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He next submits that the predecessor of the opposite party No.1-5 and opposite party No.6 instituted the instant suit for cancellation of the partition deed No.2990 dated 01.03.2009 as they are the parties/executants of the same but the petitioner Nos.1-5 substituted as 1 (Ka)-1(Uma) vide Order No. 17 dated 14.03.2013 as the legal heirs of deceased plaintiff No.1, hence the suit for cancellation of partition deed being not maintainable in the eye of law and therefore the plaint is liable to be rejected for ends of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that the learned judge of the trial Court on plain reading of the plaint ought to have considered that the parties of the instant suit being legal heirs of deceased Wahidul Hoque and the plaintiffs and others agreed to relinquish their respective shares in favour of other co-sharers and the relinquish/release was part of compromise upon family settlement vide registered deed of partition No.2990 dated 01.03.2009 and also all the parties of the suit were benefited by the transaction made between them, hence the plaintiffs are estopped from claiming their inheritance shares by cancelling the said registered deed and non consideration of this vital aspect of the suit being an error of law, the impugned order is liable to be set aside for ends of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He next submits that the plaintiffs executed the above written registered deed of partition by admitting its averments as true and correct, hence they are legally estopped by deed against the parties of the said deed and also they are debarred from denying a certain material facts asserted in it, that is why the plaint is liable to be rejected for ends of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further pointed out that on reading of the plaint as a whole of the suit it is crystal clear that the alleged registered deed of partition either is not a sale deed or a decree of a Court rather it is a family settlement deed among the co-sharers for their ancestral properties, hence it cannot be cancelled at the instance of the 2 (two) co-sharers as per provision of section 39 of the Specific Relief Act as other signatories of the said deed did not deny the execution and registration of the said deed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that the learned Judge of the trial Court should have considered that in adjudicating upon the validity of the impugned registered partition deed on the tracing the processes of enquiry before registration, admission and denial of execution endorsement of particulars etc. as evident in sections 34,35,58 and 59 respectively of the Registration Act, 1908 as invariably culminate in the granting of a certificate of registration under section 60(2) of the said Act and non consideration of this vital aspect of the suit being an error of law, the impugned order is liable to be set aside for ends of justice.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He finally submits that in exercise of its inherent power under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the Court can reject a plaint where the case is not covered by Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure for ends of justice and to prevent the abuse of the process of the Court below and accordingly he prayed for making the Rule Absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">On the other hand, Mr. M. Sadequr Rahman, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the plaintiffs-opposite parties opposes the Rule and submits that there is a settled principle of law when the plaint should be rejected and the learned Judge of the trial Court rightly rejected the application, for rejection of plaint in particular the present suit cannot be finally adjudicated without taking evidence and also this suit is not barred by any law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that whether the registered deed of partition is a sale deed or a decree of court or a family settlement deed among the co-sharers for their ancestral properties and registration and endorsement was genuine, regular and in order and the petitioner is in possession over the suit land; all these issues raised in the application for rejection of plaint can only be decided by taking evidence by the trial Court. Therefore, the instant Rule should be discharged for ends of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that it has been held in the case of Ismat Zerin Khan Vs. The World Bank and others reported in 11 MLR (AD) 58 that:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">“Plaint cannot be rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure either on the question of law or on fact before the filing of the written statement by the defendant.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He finally submits that in the instant case the defendants have not yet filed their written statements and as such he prayed for discharging the Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">We have heard the submissions of the learned Advocates of both the parties at length and perused the revisional application, the impugned order, the papers and documents as available on the record and the decisions of our Apex Court as well as of the Indian jurisdiction very carefully.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">For convenience of understanding, Order VII Rule 11 is quoted below:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">“11. The plaint shall be rejected in the following cases:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Where it does not disclose a cause of action; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Where the relief claimed is undervalued, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to correct the valuation within a time to be fixed by the Court fails to do so;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Where the relief claimed is properly valued, but the plaint is written upon paper insufficiently stamped, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to supply the requisite stamp paper within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails to do so; and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Where the suit appears from the statement in the plaint to be barred by any law.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It has been held in the case of Bangladesh Jatiya Samabaya Shilpa Samity Ltd. Vs. M/S Shan Hosiery, Proprietor Md. Abu Taleb and others, reported in 12 BLT (AD) 253, which is quoted below:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">“With regard to rejection of plaint under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the High Court Division rightly found that in deciding the question as to whether a plaint is liable to be rejected the court is always required to peruse the plaint only and court is not permitted to travel beyond the plaint to dig out grounds to reject the plaint which is a settled principle of law.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, after examining the series of decisions of our Apex Court regarding Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, we may refer some of the decisions reported in Abdul Malek Sawdagar Vs. Md. Mahbubey Alam, 57 DLR (AD)18, Nur Muhammad Vs. Mainuddin, 39DLR (AD) 1; Abul Khair (Md) Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd., 53 DLR (AD) 62, Bangladesh Shilpa Rin Sangstha Vs. Rahman Textile Mills Ltd., 51 DLR (AD) 221, Nurunnessa Vs. Mohiuddin Chowdhury 49 DLR (AD) 234, Eastern Bank Ltd Vs. Sub-Ordinate Judge, 49 DLR 531, Anath Bandhu Guha &amp; Sons Ltd. Through its Attorney Md. Sirajul Hoq Vs. Babu Sudhangshu Shekhar Halder, 42 DLR (AD) 244, Kazi (Md) Shahajahan and another Vs. Md. Khalilur Rahman Madbar and others, 54 DLR (AD) 125 and Ismat Zerin Khan Vs. the World Bank and others, 11 MLR (AD) 58, wherein the principles laid down as under:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(I)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The well settled principle of laws relating to Order VII Rule 11 are that the plaint can be rejected only on reference to plaint itself as whether it is barred in any of the four clauses of Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(II)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Plaint cannot be rejected on defense material as well as on mixed question of law and fact.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(III)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Where evidence is required and where there is material, plaint cannot be rejected.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(IV)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Plaint can be rejected if it does not disclose a cause of action and barred by any law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(V)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">There is no hard and fast Rule when an application for rejection of plaint is to be filed but ends of justice demands that it must be filed at the earliest opportunity.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 40.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(VI)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Plaint cannot be rejected before filing of the written statement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, let us focus in the Indian jurisdiction regarding the principles of rejection of plaint. In the case of M/S Crescent Petroleum Ltd Vs. Manchegorsk and another AIR 2000 Bom 161 at 168 it has been held that:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">‘This power ought to be used only when the Court is absolutely sure that the plaintiff does not have an arguable case at all. The exercise of this power though arising in Civil Procedure can be said to belong to the realm of criminal jurisprudence and any benefit of the doubt must go to the plaintiff, whose plaint is to be branded as an abuse of the process of the Court. This jurisdiction ought to be very sparingly exercised and only in very exceptional cases. The exercise of this power would not be justified merely because the story told in the pleading was highly improbable or which may be difficult to believe.’ </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, let us consider the inherent power of the Court, where a plaint may be rejected by the Court even the provisions of Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure are found not to be applicable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the case of Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islamic Bank Bangladesh Limited and others reported in 53 DLR (AD) 12, it has been held that:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">“Now it is a well settled principle of law that if the continuation of the suit is found to be an abuse of the process of the court, if the suit is foredoomed or if the ultimate result of the suit is as clear as the day light, the suit should be buried at its inception by rejecting the plaint by invoking inherent powers of the Court provided under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, on perusal of the facts of the present case, it appears to be distinguishable from the case reported in 53 DLR (AD) 12. In exceptional situation a plaint can be rejected under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure even if it does not come within the mischief of the Rule, but such situation is absent in the present case.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, keeping in mind, all the principles relating to Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, we have thoroughly gone through the plaint and considered the submissions of the learned Advocates for both the parties very carefully.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The contentions of the learned Advocate for the petitioner are that the plaint is liable to be rejected as because the alleged registered deed of partition either is not a sale deed or a decree of a court rather it is a family settlement deed among the co-sharers for their ancestral properties and cannot be cancelled at the instance of the two co-sharers as per provision of Section 39 of the Specific Relief Act and further non-consideration of the validity of the impugned registered partition deed under Section 60(2) of the Registration Act, 1908, the trial Court has committed an error of law, in our opinion all these issues have no manner of application in the present case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, the submissions of the learned Advocate for the opposite parties are that the defendants have not yet filed their written statements, are not fully correct as it appears that defendant No.12 has filed a written statement denying the averments made in the plaint. However, defendant No.3 who has filed the application for rejection of plaint did not file the written statement.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the light of the clear pronouncement of law relating to Order VII Rule 11, it is well settled principle of law that to decide the fate of a plaint under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, averments in the plaint have to be read without looking at the defense and as such whether the registered deed of partition is a sale deed or a decree of Court or a family settlement deed among the co-sharers for their ancestral properties and registration and endorsement was genuine, regular and in order and plaintiffs have no possession over the suit land rather the petitioner is in possession of the same, in our view all these issues can only <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">be decided by taking evidence by the trial Court.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It has been decided by our Apex Court in the Case of Head Mistress, Hazrat Shah Ali Girl’s High School Vs. Md. Ibrahim reported in 65 DLR (AD) 300 that, “The suit cannot be finally adjudicated without taking evidence. The High Court Division acted beyond his jurisdiction and finally adjudicated the case which he cannot do before trial and he also cannot allow the prayer of the plaintiff directly asking authority to give fresh appointment to the plaintiff from the date of dismissal.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Similar view has been expressed in the <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">recent case of Comprehensive Holdings Ltd. Vs.</span><span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> MH Khan Monju reported in 69DLR (AD) 420.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">From the above discussions, it appears that the grounds urged for in the application for rejection of plaint are absolutely the subject matter of evidence, which cannot be decided before taking evidence. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, on plain reading from the statements of plaint of the present case it is evident that the same clearly discloses the cause of action, the relief claimed is not under valued, the plaint was not written upon the paper insufficiently stamped and not barred by any other law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">36.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">So, it is our considered view that the rejection of a plaint is a serious matter and the Court has a duty to examine the plaint very carefully when considering the issues relating to Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure. It cannot be ordered without satisfying the requirement of the above said provision and only in very exceptional cases, this power should be exercised.</span></span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--> </span><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">37.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the above facts and circumstances of the case and after examining the decisions of our Apex Court as well as of the Indian Jurisdiction, we can safely come to a conclusion that the learned Court below has not committed any error of law in rejecting the application, for rejection of plaint under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, rather the learned Court below rightly passed the impugned Order dated 27.03.2014.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">38.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above discussions, we do not find any merit in the Rule.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">39.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result, the Rule is discharged without any order as to costs. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">40.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">However, since this is a long pending case, the trial court is hereby directed to dispose of the Other Suit No.09 of 2011 expeditiously, preferably within 06(six) months from the date of receipt of this judgment.    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">41.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay granted earlier by this court is hereby recalled and vacated.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">42.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate the judgment and order to the Court below at once.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 30.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__C.%20R.%203929%20of%2014_Ahmed%20Sohel,%20J.__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Civil Revision No. 3929 of 2014</span></u></strong></a></span></p></div></div><p style="text-align: justify;"> </p></div></div>
773	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Al haj Md. Fzlul Hoque Vs.  The State and another, (Jahangir Hossain, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32208 of 2018   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Jahangir Hossain, J And Md. Jahangir Hossain, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Iqbal Kabir, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Al-Haj Md. Fazlul Hoque </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State and another </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Negotiable Instruments Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(criminal miscellaneous jurisdiction)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 157px;" width="487"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 214.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 157px;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Jahangir Hossain, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">And</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Jahangir Hossain, J. </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">28.11.2018</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 37.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 157px;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%20_32208%20of%2018_Jahangir%20Hossain,%20J.__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p></td><td style="width: 191.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 157px;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Al-Haj Md. Fazlul Hoque</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Accused-Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">The State and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Opposite Parties </span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 112%;">Negotiable Instruments Act (XXVI of 1881)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%; text-align: left;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 21C</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Cheque in question may be prepared by different persons and pen but the question is whether the cheque has been signed by its owner. Admittedly, the owner i.e. drawer handed over the cheques to the opposite party No. 02 after his signature on those cheques which may be undated given by the owner to the drawer for encashment in future inserting appropriate date on the cheque in question. . . .(13)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Negotiable Instruments Act (XXVI of 1881)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Section 138</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">General Clauses Act (X of 1897)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Section 27</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">It appears from petitions of complaint that the opposite party No. 2 served legal notices through his lawyer which were received on different dates, as mentioned in the respective complaints, by the accused- petitioner. The right of filing complaint was created after expiry of 30 (thirty) days from the date of receipt of the legal notices. It also appears that the opposite party No. 2 filed complaints before the concerned magistrate court within the stipulated time as required by law. So no question of illegality is found in filing the petitions of complaint against the accused petitioner. Nevertheless, once the notice was sent by registered post with acknowledge with proper address of the recipient , there is presumption under section 27 of the General Clauses Act that the service of the notices shall be deemed to have been effected accordingly. Although Negotiable Instruments Act being a special law does not invite any other law like General Clauses Act but it is simple maxi which can be applied in service of notice in the manner as stated in section 27 of General Clauses Act].<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Section 561A </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">The date of issuance of the cheque is a question of fact to be ascertained at the time of trial. Non disclose of such fact in the petition of complaint or in the legal notice cannot offer the proceeding liable to be quashed. It is to be seen first whether the prima facie case is present on the fact of complaint-petition which constitutes and offence under section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act. It would be a great prejudice to the complaint if the proceeding is quashed at this state i.e. before proving his case by evidence Clause (a) to the provision of section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 refers to six months from the date from which the cheque was drawn not from the date the cheque was handed over. ...(15)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Negotiable Instruments Act (XXVI of 1881)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 138</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is immaterial as to whether civil dispute is present or not in connection with the transactions. The question is only the cheque which has been returned unpaid to the complaint and accordingly he sought redress by filing the above cases following the provision of the Act. He has come before the court with clean hand upon refusal of the cheques unpaid by the concerned Bank of the accused-petitioner.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . .(17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">48 DLR (AD) 213; 56 DLR (HD) 636; 2000 Criminal Law Journal 1988 and 1993; Criminal Law Journal 2359; 66 DLR (HD) 547; 1984-1997 DCR (1) 380; 17 BLC (AD) 177; 32 DLR (AD) 1 and 48 DLR (AD) 87 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-indent: -.5pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Mr. Md. Iqbal Kabir, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">. . . For the Petitioner</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-indent: -.5pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> Mr. Md. Abdul Alim Miah, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">. . . For the opposite-party No.02</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. K M Zahid Sarwar, D.A.G with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ms. Yesmin Begum Bithi, D.A.G </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. Nizamul Haque Nizam, A.A.G and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mohammad Shaheen Mirdha, A.A.G</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; text-indent: -.7pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">. . . For the State </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Jahangir Hossain, J:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></u></strong><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">This Court upon 10[ten] applications moved by the accused-petitioner under section 561-A of the Code of Criminal Procedure issued rules along with orders of stay calling upon the opposite-parties to show cause as to why the proceedings of Sessions Case Nos. 101/2017, 98/2017, 180/2017, 117/2017, 99/2017, 118/2017, 116/2017, 122/2017, 121/2017 arising out of C.R. Case Nos. 58/2017, 62/2017, 57/2017, 48/2017, 60/2017, 52/2017, 49/2017, 59/2017, 50/2017, 51/2017, 58/2017 under section 138(1) of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881, now pending in the Court of learned Sessions Judge, Thakurgaon should not be quashed and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span><u></u></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Since the parties and issues are identical, <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">these Miscellaneous Cases being Nos. 32208/2018,</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">32213/2018, 32214/2018, 32197/2018, 32198/2018, 32199/2018, 32200/2018, 32207/2018, 32713/2018, </span><span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">32845/2018 have been heard together and disposed</span> them of by passing one single judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Prosecution case, in brief, is that the opposite party No.02 as complainant filed petitions of complaint with the magistrate court on different dates alleging that through business transactions a relationship was grown up between him and the accused-petitioner. During such transactions both parties agreed to sell and purchase ‘rice bran’ from the Auto Rice Mills of accused-petitioner. Subsequently a registered deed of contract was made on 29.08.2013 between them on payment of Tk. 1,42,00,000/-[one crore forty two lakh] received by the accused-petitioner from the opposite-party No. 02 on condition to repay the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">same with effect from 15.01.2014 to 30.01.2014.</span> Failing which the accused-petitioner shall be bound to supply 35,00,500/-[thirty five lakh five hundred] sacks of </span><span style="font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS',sans-serif; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">‘</span><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">rice bran</span><span style="font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS',sans-serif; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">’</span><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> weighting 55 Kg per sack to the opposite party No. 02 within 24[twenty four] months with effect from 30.01.2014 to 30.01.2016.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">As per alternative clause of contract, the accused-petitioner supplied only 12,980[twelve thousand nine hundred eighty] sacks of ‘rice bran’ to the opposite party No. 02 instead of 35,00,500/-[thirty five lakh five hundred] sacks. As per third option of the contract the accused-petitioner would have to repay Tk-900/- for each sack of ‘rice bran’ to the opposite party No.02 on the remaining 34,87,520/- sacks.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">According to the said terms and conditions of the contract, the accused-petitioner issued ten cheques alternatively on his account of National Bank Limited, Panchagarh branch and handed over the same to the opposite party No. 02 as security. Failing to fulfill all the conditions mentioned above, the cheque being Nos. NDC/F-7817833, NDC/F-7817829, NDC/F-7817828, NDC/F-7817825, NDC/F-7817826, NDC/F-7817831, NDC/F-7817830, NDC/F-7817834, NDC/F-7817827, given by the accused-petitioner, were presented to the Uttara Bank Limited, Thakurgaon Branch on different dates for encashment. But the cheques in question were returned unpaid from the Bank of the accused-petitioner due to insufficiency of found as stated in the dishonored slips. Thereafter, the opposite party No. 02 sent legal notices to the accused-petitioner through his engaged lawyer on different occasions [according to dishonored dates] requesting him to repay the amount of dishonored cheques within thirty days. The accused-petitioner received the notices on different occasions as mentioned in the respective petition of complaint but did not pay heed to repay the amounts. Hence, the cases were started against the accused-petitioner under section 138(1) of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">In support of the Rules, Mr. Md. Iqbal Kabir, learned Advocate contends that as security ten undated cheques were issued by the accused-petitioner and handed the same over to the opposite party No. 02 on the day of 29.08.2013 when a registered deed of contract was executed. Subsequently, the figure of the amount has been written on each cheque by different persons and pen and undated cheques after being filled up, have been placed in the bank after around 3½ years from the time the cheques have been handed over. It is further submitted that admittedly 12,980 sacks of ‘rice bran’ were supplied to the opposite party No. 02 towards part payment of the cheques issued by the accused-petitioner. The cost of the said sacks of ‘rice bran’ stands Tk. 1,16,82,000/-[one crore sixteen lakh eighty two thousand] as per Tk. 900 for each. In that view of the fact remaining money stands [1,42,00,000-1,16,82,000]= Tk. 25,18,000/-only and the amount shown in those cheques is higher than the amount due. If a cheque is placed by showing higher amount, than the amount due or payable due to dishonor, the cheques in question would not create any cause of action under section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;
