mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">It is further contended that it is a mandatory provision to mention in the complaint as to when the cheque was issued but in the present cases as per section 138(1)(a) of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 the complainant did not mention the issuing dates of the cheques. </span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Learned Advocate finally submits that as per decision, reported in 48 DLR(AD) 213, para-14 the petitions of complaint, examination of complainant, registered deed of contract dated 29.08.2013 as mentioned in the complaint petitions and order of declining or inclining to frame charges are the materials of the prosecution which can be scrutinized by this Court under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">In support of these contentions he has also cited some more decisions namely, 56 DLR (HD) 636, 48 DLR (AD) 213, 2000 Criminal Law Journal, Page-1988, 1993 Criminal Law Journal, Page-2359, 66 DLR (HD)547, 1984-1997 DCR (1)380, 17 BLC (AD)177, 32 DLR(AD)1 and 48 DLR(AD)87.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Mr. K M Zahid Sarwar along with Ms. Yesmin Begum Bithi, learned Deputy Attorney Generals, Mr. Nizamul Huq @ Nizam and Mr. Mohammad Shaheen Mridha, learned Assistant Attorney Generals appearing on behalf of the State-opposite party opposes the Rules.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">On the contrary, Mr. Md. Abdul Alim Miah, learned Advocate appearing for the opposite party No.02 by filing affidavits-in-opposition submits that a criminal proceeding cannot be quashed on the basis of defence materials which are still not part of the materials for the prosecution [48 DLR(AD) 213]. Ante-dated cheque written by different person and pen as alleged by the accused-petitioner is a disputed question of facts which cannot be looked in by the High Court Division under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure and the rules issued by this Hon’ble Court are liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">In the instant cases many issues have been raised by the accused-petitioner but it is to be borne in mind that the opposite party No. 02 as complainant brought the allegation against the accused-petitioner under section 138(1) of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 for dishonored cheques issued by the accused-petitioner earlier in favour of the opposite party No. 02 due to insufficiency of fund. So we should confine ourselves within the purview of `the Act [Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881] which is, no doubt, a special law as pointed out by the learned Advocate for the accused-petitioner. Now it is to be seen as to whether the complainant has violated any provisions of this Act in filing the complaint cases. The object of the contract was that the terms and conditions were to be fulfilled by the accused-petitioner within the stipulated time, as mentioned in the contract. If once failed to do so, the complainant would have the right to place by inserting dates in the cheques for encashment. The issued cheques without date will be treated as inchoate immature documents handed over to the payee with implied authority to pen the date on the cheques in question. The drawer of the cheque only can chose and decide to hand over dated, post-dated or undated cheque to the payee. But he cannot eventually come forward with a plea that undated cheque was given to the payee who is not allowed to present the cheque to the bank for encashment by putting date on it. Section 21C of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 is very much clear that, </span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">“21C. Anti-dating and post-dating- A promissory note, bill of exchange or cheque is not invalid by reason only that it is ante-dated or post-dated:</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Provided that the ante-dating or post-dating does not involve any illegal or fraudulent purpose or transaction.”</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Cheques in question may be prepared by different persons and pen but the question is whether the cheque has been signed by its owner. Admittedly, the owner i.e. drawer handed over the cheques to the opposite party No. 02 after his signature on those cheques which may be undated given by the owner to the drawer for encashment in future inserting appropriate date on the cheques in question.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">It appears from petitions of complaint that the opposite party No. 02 served legal notices through his lawyer which were received on different dates, as mentioned in the respective complaints, by the accused-petitioner. The right of filing complaint was created after expiry of 30[thirty] days from the date of receipt of the legal notices. It also appears that the opposite party No. 02 filed complaints before the concerned magistrate court within the stipulated time as required by law. So no question of illegality is found in filing the petitions of complaint against the accused-petitioner. Nevertheless, once the notice was sent by registered post with acknowledgement with proper address of the recipient, there is presumption under section 27 of the General Clauses Act that the service of the notices shall be deemed to have been effected accordingly [although Negotiable Instruments Act being a special law does not invite any other law like General Clauses Act but it is a simple maxim which can be applied in service of notice in the manner as stated in section 27 of General Clauses Act]. The complainant [opposite party No. 02] also complied with the provision of section 138[I](a) of the Negotiable Instruments Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">However, the date of issuance of the cheque is a question of fact to be ascertained at the time of trial. Non-disclosure of such fact in the petition of complaint or in the legal notice cannot offer the proceeding liable to be quashed. It is to be seen first whether the prima faci case is present on the face of complaint-petition which constitutes an offence under section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act. <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">It would be a great prejudice to the complainant</span> if the proceeding is quashed at this stage i.e. before proving his case by evidence. Clause (a) to the provision of section 138[1] of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 refers to six months from the date from which the cheque was drawn not from the date the cheque was handed over.</span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level3 lfo2; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Here in this case; I have come across from the proposed amendment of the written statement that the fundamental character of the defendant-appellant’s earlier case would not be changed in any manner, if the proposed amendment of written statement come into force and the proposed amendment is definitely required for determining the real question of controversy between the parties to the original suit for partition.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level3 lfo2; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having regard to the facts, circumstances and the discussions referred to above, I am constrained to hold such a view that the learned court of appeal below was not lawful in disallowing the application for acceptance of the additional written statement and in the impugned judgment and order there has been non application of judicial mind in giving some premature observation and findings on the sub-kabala deed No.20518 dated 15.11.1968.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level3 lfo2; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the result, the Rule having sufficient merit is made absolute without any order as to costs. The impugned order dated 08.06.2015 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, 2<sup>nd</sup> Court, Bogura in Partition Appeal No.147 of 1997 is hereby set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">36.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Communicate the judgment and order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%20_32208%20of%2018_Jahangir%20Hossain,%20J.__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;"> 32208 of 2018</span></u></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;"> With </span></strong><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32213 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32214 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32197 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32198 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32199 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32200 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32207 of 2018; Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32713 of 2018 and Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 32845 of 2018.</span></p></div></div></div></div>
774	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Alhaj Md. Mizanur Rahman Vs.  M.D. and C.E.O Agrani Bank, (Syed Md.Ziaul Karim, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> First Appeal No. 278 of 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J And Sheikh Md. Zakir Hossain, J. </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Shafique Ahmed, Senior Advocate, with Mr. Khair Ezaz Maswood, Advocate, Mr. Mahbub Shafique, Advocate, and Mr. Md. Humayun Bashar, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Alhaj Md. Mizanur Rahman</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Managing Director and C.E.O. Agrani Bank Ltd. and another  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Arbitration Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 249px;" width="551"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 243.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 249px;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; font-style: normal;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">And</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Sheikh Md. Mizanur Rahman</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . .Plaintiff-Appellant</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Managing Director and C.E.O. Agrani Bank Ltd. and another </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . .Defenant-Respondents</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Sections 7 and 10</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;">If sections 7 and 10</span> of the Arbitration Act are read together the intention of the legislature becomes clearer that once the parties to a contract agreed to settle their disputes that may arise out of execution of the contract they must be encouraged and directed to follow the procedure what they agreed to, and the Court should not proceed with any civil proceedings commenced by one party against other party in respect of any matter covered by such arbitration agreement. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                      </span>. . .(26)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Order VII, Rule 11(d)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">All the facts and submissions of the learned Counsel of both the parties indicate that the plaint of the suit should not be rejected under Order VII Rule 11 (d) of the Code, where there is an arbitration clause in agreement to dissolve the dispute by Arbitration and parties are willing to go for Arbitration. In view of such facts the ends of justice would best be served if we direct the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">plaintiff appellant and defendant respondent</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> no.1 to dissolve their dispute by Arbitration and in accordance with the Arbitration Act 2001. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above, the Court below without considering the materials on record and aforesaid principles of law, by rejecting the plaint of the suit committed an error of law. Therefore, the impugned judgment and decree of the Court below is liable to be interfered by the High Court Division.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                     </span></span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . (25, 27 and 28)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ratan Chand Dharam Chand Vs. The Secretary of State for India in Council and another 18 CWN 1340, AIR 1928 Oudh 495; Screedam Chandra Bhur Vs. Tencori Mukherjee and others AIR 1953 Cal. 222; Sundar Ali being dead his heirs: Mannan and others Vs. Md. Serajul Islam Sarker and others 56 DLR (AD) 210; Abul Malek Sawdagar Vs. Md. Mahbubey Alam and others 57 DLR (AD) 18; Abul Khair Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and another 21 BlD (AD) 32, 53 DLR (AD) 62; Afzal Hossain Diptee Vs. Radha Kanta Korati and others 15 BLC 196; Bangladesh Water Development Board Vs. Contractor, Manu Barrage 9 BLT 21 and Shafi A. Chowdhury Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and another 54 DLR 310 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.25pt 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mr. Shafique Ahmed, Senior Advocate, with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.25pt 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mr. Khair Ezaz Maswood, Advocate,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.25pt 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mr. Mahbub Shafique, Advocate, and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mr. Md. Humayun Bashar, Advocate,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the plaintiff-appellant</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.25pt 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mr. Mohammad Mehedi Hasan Chowdhury, Advocate With</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.25pt 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Mrs. Jausna Perveen, Advocate, and </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Rokonuzzaman Prince, Advocate,<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                            </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">.. . For the defendant no.1 respondent.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">No one appears,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>proforma defendant no.2-Respondent.</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">By this appeal, the plaintiff appellant has challenged the legality and propriety of the judgment and decree dated 26-09-2017 passed by learned Joint District Judge, Fifth Court, Dhaka, rejecting the plaint of Title Suit no. 326 of 2017 under Order VII Rule 11(d) of the Code of Civil Procedure (briefly as the Code). </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Material facts leading to this appeal are that on 26-09-2017 the appellant as plaintiff instituted Title Suit no. 326 of 2017 in the Fifth Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka impleading the respondents as defendants for realization of arrear of rents for Tk. 205,24,45,760/-, mandatory injunction and compensation. The relieves claimed in suit reads as hereunder: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-indent: 9pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; text-indent: 9pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;
