text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In suit, on 26-09-2017 the plaintiff filed an application under Order XXXIX Rules 1 and 2 and Section 151 of the Code for temporary injunction restraining the defendant no. 1 from removing furniture from the suit premises without paying the arrear rents for Tk. 205,24,45,760/-.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">After hearing the learned Judge by the impugned order dated 26-09-2017 rejected the plaint of the suit under Order VII Rule 11 (d) of the Code as the suit is barred under Section 7 of the Arbitration Act 2001. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Feeling aggrieved the plaintiff as appellant preferred the instant appeal.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing for the appellant seeks to impeach the impugned judgment and decree on two fold arguments:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Firstly</span></u></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The defendant no.1 is his tenant and both the parties entered into an agreement on 20-02-2013. In the said agreement there is an Arbitration Clause wherein it has been stated that if any dispute arises between the parties the dispute should be referred for Arbitration and the same should be dissolved therein pursuant to the Arbitration Act 2001. So the learned Judge without giving the plaintiff any scope to resolve the matter in Arbitration rejected the plaint which caused a serious miscarriage of justice. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Second and lastly: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The plaint clearly discloses the cause of action and from plain reading of the plaint it appears that there is no such statement that the suit is barred under law so the plaint cannot be rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code but <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">t</span>he learned Judge of the Court below without considering such law and facts dismissed the suit which is absolutely contrary to law. Moreso, the plaintiff is willing to dissolve the matter in dispute with the defendant no.1 by Arbitration and in accordance with Arbitration Act 2001 but the learned Judge without giving him any scope to take such step rejected the plaint which cannot be sustained in the eye of law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing for the respondent no.1 candidly submits that the learned Judge of the Court below without rejecting the plaint could give an opportunity to plaintiff to dissolve the matter in issue by arbitration. He lastly submits that the defendant no. 1 is also willing to dissolve the matter-in-issue by Arbitration. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate their submissions we have gone through the records and given our anxious consideration to their submissions. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The point for consideration whether the impugned judgment and decree calls for interference by this Court. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">For the convenience of understanding the provisions of Order VII rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure reads as hereunder:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">″ 11- The plaint shall be rejected on the following issues:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Where it does not disclose a cause of action.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the relief claimed is undervalued, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to correct the valuation within a time to be fixed by the Court fails to do so;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the relief claimed is properly valued, but the plaint is written upon paper insufficiently stamped and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to supply the requisite stamp-paper within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails do so.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the suit appears from the statement in the plaint to be barred by any law.</span></em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">″</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; text-indent: 22.5pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Provided that the time fixed by the Court for the correction of the valuation or supplying of the requisite stamp-paper shall not exceed twenty one days. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On going to the materials on record it transpires that the plaintiff instituted Title Suit no.326 of 2017 for realisation of money for Tk.205,24,45,760/- from the defendant no.1, mandatory injunction compensation. The only point assigned in impugned order that the suit is barred under law i.e. under Arbitration Act. The question whether the plaint is liable to be rejected being barred by law must be apparent from the statement made in the plaint itself and not from the written statement or any other material other than that has been put in the plaint.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">From the plain reading of the statements of plaint of the instant suit it is evident that the same clearly discloses the cause of action; the relief claimed is not undervalued; the plaint was not written upon paper insufficiently stamped; from the statement of the plaint it does not appear that the suit is barred by any law. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Now coming to clause (d) of rule 11, it appears that clause (d) of the rule authorise the rejection of a plaint when the suit appears from the statements in the plaint to be barred by any law. This clause applies when it appear from the statements in the plaint that the suit is barred but it has no application where there is no clear or specific admission in the plaint suggesting that the suit is barred. This clause is attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. As for instance when from the statements made in the plaint it appears that the cause of action arose beyond the period of limitation fixed under the statute and no indication is given that limitation has been saved, the plaint may be rejected. In a proper case, when it appears to be barred by limitation, the plaint may be allowed to be amended without rejection. It is not mandatory for the Court to reject the pliant. It may ask the plaintiff to amend it so as to make suit maintainable. Where the plaintiff does not comply with such an order the Court may reject the plaint. Reference may be made to the cases reported in 18 CWN 1340.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>AIR 1928 Oudh 495 and AIR 1953 Cal.222.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Ratan Chand Dharam Chand Vs. The Secretary of State for India in Council and another, reported in 18 CWN 1340, a Division Bench of Calcutta High Court while considering the scope of Order VII, rule 11(d) observed as follows:-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">′′ That rule obviously has no application, for there was no statement in the plaint which suggested that the suit was barred. On the contrary it was specifically stated that notice under sec. 80 had been served on the ′′Collector′′ without specifying the district. The defect was not discovered till after the defendants had entered appearance and it was then too late to reject the plaint ′′. </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Similarly in the case of Maqsood Ali Vs. Deputy Commissioner, Bara Banki and another, reported in A.I.R. 1928, Oudh, 495, a Division Bench of Oudh held that if the suit was not on the face of it barred by any law, Order VII, rule 11(d) had no application. The relevant portion of the judgment ran as follows: </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">′′ We do not consider that the suit appeared from the statement in the plaint to be barred by law and we do not think that rule had any application. He has pointed out to us that in a suit which was filed in a similar manner a Bench of the Allahabad High Court stated in Nachhu Vs. Secy. of State that the plaint ought to have been rejected under the proviso of s. 54(c) of the old Code of Civil Procedure, that clause was exactly the same as Order VII rule 11(d). The learned Judge composing the Bench gave no reasons for this conclusion and did not give any effect to it for we find that the suit with which they were concerned had been dismissed but the Subordinate Judge and as their order was an order dismissing the appeal, the plaint was apparently not rejected. Their Lordships said : ′′ It ought to have been rejected′′ but gave no effect to that view. We have only to note in respect of this point that exactly the same question could have been raised in Bhagchand Dagadusa Vs. Secy. of State. There the suit had been dismissed by the District Judge. The appeal had been dismissed by the High Court and the appeal was again dismissed by their Lordships of the Judicial Committee. It was not there suggested that the proper procedure was to reject the plaint. In a case such as this we are of opinion that the suit is not on the face of it barred by law. The very arguments which have been advanced in appeal show that the suit on the face of it is not barred by law, as the suit has been found to be a suit that has to be dismissed after consideration of the legal arguments. Therefore we are unable to accept this view of the learned Counsel.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The Calcutta High Court in the case of Sreedam Chandra Bhur Vs. Tencori Mukherjee and others reported in A.I.R. 1953 Cal. 222 also held that Order VII rule 11(d) was attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit was prima facie barred. The Division Bench in this connection observed as follows:-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.35pt; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">′′ This clause is attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. As for instance when from the statements made in the plaint it appears that the cause of action arose beyond period of limitation fixed under the statute and no indication is given that limitation has been saved, the plaint may be rejected. Even in such a case, an opportunity is to be given to the plaintiff to amend the plaint by setting out an acknowledgement in writing signed by the defendant within the period of limitation if it is so prayed, and that without passing an order for rejection of the plaint. ‘Gunnaji Bhavaji Vs. Makanji<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Khoosal Chand’, 34 Bom. 250. As was observed in ‘Ratan Chand V. Secy. of State 18 Cal. WN 1340, action is to be taken under Or. VII, r. 11 of the Code of civil Procedure only if there is a clear and specific admission in the plaint from which it follows that the suit is barred. Reference may also be made to the observations of this Court.’ Prankrishna Vs, Kripannath’. 21 Cal. WN 209 held:</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 49.5pt; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">″ Let us now consider whether on the plaint as filed the Court will be justified in rejecting in limine the plaint under cl.(d), r.11, Or. VII, Civil P.C.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In the body of the pliant there is no admission for the Council of the Assembly is the Government under s. 80, Civil P.C. On the other hand, it is seriously contested on behalf of the plaintiff that neither of the two bodies can even be deemed to be the government. The learned Subordinate Judge refers to his order vaguely to the Trend of French Statutes conferring greater and greater powers on the French Settlement in India and creating a ′Council du Government′ there and later a cutting out Chandernagore from the Federation and conferring on Chandernagore all those powers with a separate .delegate of the ‘Commissionaire de la re-oblique, it is evident that the Chandernagore administration is a government in the grammatical and ordinary sense of the word though its functions may fall short of the those of the Governments existing in India. </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 49.5pt; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We do not think it necessary to refer to other points urged before us by the contending parties. Suffice it to say that the question whether even if the Code of Civil Procedure applies, whether s. 80 would be attracted or not cannot be decided merely on the plaint as it stands. The Court should have registered the plaint, issued notices on the defendants and allowed them to file their written statements. After issues were raised it would have been open to the Court to take up one or more of the issues as preliminary ones and decide the same. Objection that had been raised by the Court ‘suo -motu’ and such other objection as may be raised by the defendants would have to be tried on the merits, and only after <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">all the necessary facts and materials</span> are brought before the Court. ′′</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">There is no reason to differ from the above principles of law. In the instant case, there is nothing on record to show that on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. So the rule 11(d) is not at all attracted here and the plaint cannot be rejected on that score. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Sundar Ali being dead his heirs: Mannan and others Vs. Md. Serajul Islam Sarker and others 56 DLR(AD) 210 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>″<em> For the ascertainment of the cause of action the Court is required to read the plaint in its entirety.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In the case of Abdul Malek Sawdagar Vs. Md. Mahbubey Alam and others 57 DLR(AD) 18 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">″<em>The question whether the plaint is liable to be rejected being barred by law must be apparent from the statement made in the plaint itself and not from the written statement or any other material other than that has been put in the plaint. </em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Md. Abul Khair Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and another 21 BLD (AD)32=53 DLR (AD) 62 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>Where in a suit an application under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code is filed for rejecting the plaint on the ground that the averments made in the plaint do no disclose a cause of action for the suit, the Court is not called upon to decide the suit on merit on taking evidence. It is only the averment made in the plaint which are to be considered to come to a finding as to whether those disclose a cause of action. The Court while deciding such application is not permitted in law to travel beyond the averments made in the plaint. </span></em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">″</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Afzal Hossain Diptee Vs. Radha Kanta Korati and others 15 BLC 196 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">“Code of Civil Procedure</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Order VII rule 11</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 9pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On going to materials on record it transpires that the grounds urged for rejection of the plaint are absolutely the subject matter of evidence, which cannot be decided before taking evidence. On plain reading of the statements of the plaint it is evident that the same clearly discloses the cause of action, the relief claimed is not under valued, the plaint was not written upon paper insufficiently stamped and not barred by any other law. The question whether the plaint is liable to be rejected being barred by law must be apparent from the statement made in the plaint itself and not from the written statement or any other material other than that has been put in the plaint.” </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Bangladesh Water Development Board Vs. Contractor, Manu Barrage 9 BLT 21 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“Arbitration Act, 1940</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section -32</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Whether the suit instituted in presence of the arbitration agreement is maintainable.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Held: We find no such provisions in the Act barring a suit on the ground of existence of an arbitration agreement.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Shafi A. Chowdhury Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and others 54 DLR 310 held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Section 11 &amp; Order VII rule 11<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of the Code.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ordinarily, a plaint should not be rejected under Order VII rule 11 of the Code on the ground of res judicata unless it is so palpably clear and obvious from a meaningful reading of the plaint that no further evidence is required.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts indicate that the plaintiff instituted the suit for realisation of arrear rents, mandatory injection and for compensation against the defendant no.1. It is pertinent to point out that that the plaintiff entered into a tenancy agreement with defendant no.1 on 20-02-2013. In the said agreement both the parties were agreed to dissolve their matter in dispute by Arbitration and in accordance to Arbitration Act 2001. The terms of the clause of the agreement reads as hereunder:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 13.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“In the event of any dispute of any difference (s) arising out of the clauses of the terms and conditions mentioned thereinabove, such dispute of difference (s) shall be referred to the arbitration or arbitrators, one to be appointed by each Part: (Lessor and Lessee)), and a third Arbitrator/Umpire to be appointed by the mutual consent of the Two Arbitrators so appointed by the parties. Such arbitration shall be in accordance with and subject to the provisions of the Arbitration Act, 2001 and the rules thereunder, and the awards made by the arbitrators shall be final and binding upon both the LESSOR and the LESSEE.”<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">We find that the learned Advocates of both appellant and respondent no.1 candidly submit that they are willing to dissolve the matter in dispute by Arbitration and in accordance with the Arbitration Act 2001. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">All the facts and submissions of the learned Counsel of both the parties indicate that the plaint of the suit should not be rejected under Order VII Rule 11 (d) of the Code, where there is an arbitration clause in agreement to dissolve the dispute by Arbitration and parties are willing to go for Arbitration. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">If sections 7 and 10 of the Arbitration Act are read together the intention of the legislature becomes clearer that once the parties to a contract agreed to settle their disputes that may arise out of execution of the contract they must be encouraged and directed to follow the procedure what they agreed to, and the Court should not proceed with any civil proceedings commenced by one party against other party in respect of any matter covered by such arbitration agreement.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In view of such facts the ends of justice would best to serve if we direct the plaintiff appellant and defendant respondent no.1 to dissolve their dispute by Arbitration and in accordance with the Arbitration Act 2001.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above, the Court below without considering the materials on record and aforesaid principles of law, by rejecting the plaint of the suit committed an error of law. Therefore, the impugned judgment and decree of the Court below is liable to be interfered by the High Court Division.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Moreover the impugned order in its entirety is not well founded in the facts and circumstances of the case. So, the submissions advanced by the learned Counsel for the appellant prevails and appears to have a good deal of force. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the light of discussions made above and the preponderant judicial views emerging out of the authorities referred to above, we are of the view that the impugned judgment and decree suffers from legal infirmities which calls for interference by this Court. Thus the appeal having merit succeeds.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the view of foregoing narrative, the appeal is allowed. The impugned judgment and decree dated 26-09-2017 passed by learned Joint District Judge, fifth Court, Dhaka in Title Suit no. 326 of 2017 is hereby set-aside. The learned Judge of the Court below shall direct the plaintiff and defendant no.1 to take every possible step to dissolve their matter in dispute by Arbitration and in accordance with the Arbitration Act 2001 within three months, from the date of receipt of this order and till then the further proceeding of the suit shall be stayed. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The office is directed to communicate the order at once.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__F.%20A%20_278%20of%2017_Syed%20Md.%20Ziaul%20Karim%20J.__6.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">First Appeal No. 278 of 2017</span></u></strong></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
775	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Aminur Rashid Khan Vs.  Bangladesh Agricultural Development, (Md. Nuruzzaman , J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 3887 of 2016  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Nuruzzaman, J And S.H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Md. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, Advocate  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Aminur Rashid Khan </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Bangladesh Agricultural Development Corporation </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Arbitration Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 223px;" width="488"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 213.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; font-style: normal;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">And</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">S.H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J. </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">31.05.2018</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 37.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__July__2019(2)/Issue%20__July__19(2)__C.%20R.%203887%20of%2016_Md.%20Nuruzzaman,%20J.__8.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 193.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Aminur Rashid Khan</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Bangladesh Agricultural Development Corporation</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . Opposite party</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 12(4)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We are of the view that the 1<sup>st</sup> direction to appoint a sole Arbitrator by the Chairman BADC as directed by the learned District Judge seems to us not well founded in accordance with law therefore, replacement of another Arbitrator by the learned District Judge in spite of earlier Arbitrator also cannot be sustained in accordance with law. Accordingly Mr. Justice Md. Abdul Wahab Miah, the Hon’ble Judge of the Appellate </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> was appointed as a sole Arbitrator to resolve the dispute. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span>. . . (18, 24 and 30)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 115%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; color: #000000; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Md. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 115%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; color: #000000;">Mr. Md. Mojibur Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the Opposite party</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 25.25pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On an application under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure the instant Rule was issued calling upon the opposite party to show cause as to why the order No. 50 dated 24.08.16 passed by District Judge, Dhaka in Arbitration Misc. Case No. 343 of 2009 should not be set aside and/or such other or further order or orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The material facts, relevant for, disposal of the instant Rule, in short, as has been derived from the revision application, are that, in pursuant to tender No. Pur/Fert/ TSP/64/2008-09 dated 06.05.2008 floated by the opposite party for purchasing of 25,000 metric tons (MT) (±5%) of Triple Super Phosphate (TSP) fertilizer in bag, the petitioner submitted its bid dated 17.06.2008 offering to supply the same of Moroccan origin at a price of US$ 1,295.00 per MT CFR Chittagong on linear term basis, which was accepted by the opposite party’s vide letter dated 13.07.2008, following which the petitioner submitted bank guarantee No. 203GPBN081980001 dated 16.07.2008 for US$ 3,237,500.00 (United States Dollars Three Million, Two Hundred Thirty Seven Thousand Five Hundred) which constituted 10% of the total CFR value of the fertilizer, issued by Dhaka Bank Ltd., Foreign Exchange Branch, as performance guarantee to the opposite party under cover of its letter dated 16.07.2008.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioner commenced Arbitration due to dispute against the opposite party under Clause 40 of the contract made between them by sending an arbitration notice dated 16.02.2009. However, the opposite party’s Chairman failed to appoint any Arbitrator.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioner filed an application under section 12(4) of the Arbitration Act, 2001 before the learned District Judge, Dhaka for appointment of an Arbitrator which was registered as Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No.343 of 2009.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioner being aggrieved by an order dated 24.08.2016 preferred the instant revision application before this Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh and obtained the instant Rule with an order of stay. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner has submitted that the Court below committed an error of law resulting in an error in the impugned order occasioning failure of justice in allowing the opposite party’s application dated 24.08.2016 for appointment of its own employee, Mr. Md. Abdul Zalil, Member Director (Minor Irrigation), BADC, as the sole Arbitrator to arbitrate disputes between the petitioner and the opposite party without having due regard and in not considering the independence and impartiality of the said Arbitrator which is required under section 12(9) of the Arbitration Act, 2001.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">He has further submitted that the Court below committed an error of law resulting in an error in the order occasioning a failure of justice inasmuch as in passing the impugned order ex-parte without hearing the petitioner, hence, the petitioner had no opportunity to raise its objection against the appointment of the opposite party’s employee as the sole Arbitrator and, as such, the impugned order is liable to be set aside. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">He has argued that the learned District Judge committed an error of law resulting in an error in the impugned order occasioning failure of justice without appreciating that the sole Arbitrator appointed by the Opposite Party for arbitrating the disputes of itself own Corporation wherein he is an Officer under that Corporation and the petitioner, which gives rise to justifiable doubts with respect to his independence and impartiality. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">He in a same breath has argued that the learned District Judge committed an error of law resulting in an error in the order occasioning failure of justice as the Court below has completely failed to apply its judicial mind in passing the impugned order allowing the appointment of the opposite party’s officer as Arbitrator for arbitrating disputes between its Corporation and the petitioner in clear violation of the provision of sub-section 9 of the section 12 of the Arbitration Act, 2001 and, as such, the impugned judgment and order is liable to the set aside.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The opposite party contested the Rule by filing counter affidavit stating, inter-alia, that the opposite party in compliance of the Court’s Order dated 17.01.2016 appointed Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain, NDC, Member Director (Fertilizer Management), BADC, Dhaka as the sole Arbitrator on 07.06.2016. Thereafter, the said Arbitrator Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain informed the Chairman of BADC and he has been transferred to Jibon Bima Corporation and, as such, he would not be able to perform the functions of the Arbitrator. The Chairman of BADC was intimated the said information vide letter dated 02.08.2016. Hence, the Chairman of BADC appointed Mr. Md. Abdul Jalil, Member Director (Minor Irrigation) of BADC, Dhaka in place of Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain, NDC as a sole Arbitrator on 16.08.2016 and communicated the same to the petitioner as well as the Hon’ble District Judge, Dhaka by letter dated 14.08.2016.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It has been contended in the counter affidavit that the petitioner, never-ever raised any question against the first appointment of sole Arbitrator, therefore, instead of first Arbitrator, appointment of 2<sup>nd</sup> Arbitrator in place of Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain was bonafide and lawful. Therefore, the objection raised by the petitioner regarding the appointment of 2<sup>nd</sup> Arbitrator Mr. Md. Abdul Jalil, Member Director (Minor Irrigation) of BADC, Dhaka neither illegal nor suffers from any legal infirmity. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Mojibur Rahman, the learned Advocate for the opposite party has submitted that the appointment of the 1<sup>st</sup> Arbitrator Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain has not been challenged by the petitioner. Therefore, instead of 1<sup>st</sup> Arbitrator Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain appointment of Mr. Md. Abdul Jalil as 2<sup>nd</sup> Arbitrator cannot be questioned by the petitioner. The Chairman of BADC has appointed the Arbitrator by dint of Arbitration Clause 40.1 of the Contract made between the parties therefore, in passing the impugned order the learned District Judge, Dhaka committed no error or law and, as such, no interference calls for by this Court. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have considered the submissions advanced by the learned Advocates of the respective parties. We have perused the impugned order dated 17.01.2016 passed by the learned District Judge, Dhaka. We have also perused the application under section 12(4) of the Arbitration Act, 2001 for appointment of Arbitrator and the agreement dated 22.07.2008 made between the parties. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On a careful reading of clause 40.1 of the agreement it appears that there is a provision for appointment of Arbitrator by the Chairman of BADC, if any, dispute arises in between the parties in term of the agreement. It appears from the application for appointment of Arbitrator the petitioner on 16.02.2009 sent a notice to the Opposite Party under clause 40 of the Contract for appointment of Arbitrator. However, the Chairman of BADC failed to appoint any Arbitrator. Therefore, the present petitioner for appointment of Arbitrator invokes the provision of section 12(4) of the Arbitration Act, 2001. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The opposite party BADC contested the Miscellaneous Case by filing written objection. On 17.01.2016 the learned District Judge directed the Chairman of BADC <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">to nominate a competent sole Arbitrator within 60 days from the date of receipt of the order.</em> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have perused the materials on record as annexed with revisional application which is annexure “<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">C</strong>” from which it is divulged that the Chairman of BADC never intimating the Court that he had nominated any person as a sole Arbitrator nor communicate the same to the learned District Judge. However, instead of appointment the Arbitrator on 24.08.2016 the opposite party BADC filed an application to appoint Mr. Md. Abdul Jalil, Member Director of BADC to appoint him as Arbitrator in place of earlier Arbitrator Mr. Md. Mofajjal Hossain. Hence, the learned District Judge by the impugned judgment and order allowed the application appointing Mr. Md. Abdul Jalil as Arbitrator. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">To appreciate the impugned order we are of the view that the provision of section 12 may be reproduced hereinbelow for the convenience and ready reference of the discussion which would be beneficial to form a legal opinion – </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt;
