No. 1255/18)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.4pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Shahjahan and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.4pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">. . . <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>Respondents</u></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt -.4pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In Cr.P. No. 1385/18)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.4pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Aminur Rahman and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.4pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">. . . <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>Respondents</u></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.4pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In Cr.P. No. 378/19)</span></em></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12pt 0.85pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 498</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The horizon of human rights is expanding all over the world, at the same time, crime rate is also increasing. Of late, this Court has been receiving repeated complaints about the violation of human rights because of indiscriminate arrest by the police. We need </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">to strike the right balance between the two. The</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> order of granting or refusing of anticip-<span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">atory bail must reflect perfect </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">balance between the two conflicting interests,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> namely, sanctity of individual liberty and the interest of the informant and society. Therefore, realistic </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">approach must be made in this regard. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                                    </span>. . .(3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Chapter XIV and Section 498</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Arrest is a part of the process of investigation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> intended to secure several purposes. It is the obligation that the accused shall make himself available for interrogation by the investigating officer as and when required. Normally the Court should not interfere with the process of investigation in any way. The accused may have to be questioned in detail regarding various facts, motive, preparation, commission and aftermath of the crime and the connection of other persons, if any, in the crime. There may be circumstances in which the accused may provide information leading to discovery of material facts. It may be necessary to curtail </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">his freedom in order to enable the investigation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> to proceed without hindrance and to protect witnesses and persons connected with the victim of the crime, to prevent his disappe-arance, to maintain law and order in </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the locality. For those or other reasons, arrest</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">may become an inevitable part of the process</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of investigation.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span>. . . (48)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Constitutions of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Article 32</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The protection of personal liberty stands expanded to make the right to life or personal liberty save in accordance with law under Article 32 of the Constitution. The language of this article itself recording of an exception indicating thereby that a person may be deprived of his liberty in accordance with the procedure established by law. It is also to be remembered always that personal liberty is a very precious fundamental right and it should be curtailed only when it becomes imperative according to the facts and circumstances of the case. Every arrest must be in accordance with the procedure establish by law. Personal liberty deprived when bail is refused, is too precious a value of our constitutional system recognised under Article 32 that the crucial power to negate it is a great trust exercisable, not casually but judicially. . . . (48)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Chapter VI B-Warrant of arrest and </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 498</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The law of arrest is one of balancing individual rights, liberties and privileges, on the one hand, and individual duties, obligations and responsibilities on the other; </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">of weighing and balancing the rights, liberties</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> and privileges of the single individual and those of individuals collectively of simply deciding what is wanted and where to put the weight and emphasis; of deciding which comes first- the criminal or society; the law violator or the law abider; of meting the challenge which Cardozo so forthrightly met when he wrestled with a similar task of balancing individual rights against society’s rights and wisely held that the exclusion rule was bad in law, the society came first, and that the criminal should not go free because the constable blundered.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>. . . (49)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 0.85pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 498</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">No inflexible guidelines or straitjacket formula can be provided for grant or refusal of anticipatory bail. No attempt should be </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">made to provide right and inflexible guidelines</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> in this respect because all circumstances and </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">situations of future can not be clearly visualised</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> for the grant or refusal of anticipatory bail. Few principles for grant of anticipatory bail can be summarised as follows:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(i) The F.I.R. lodged against the accused needs to be thoroughly and carefully examined;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(ii) The gravity of the allegation and the exact role of the accused </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">must be properly comprehended;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iii) The danger of the accused absconding if anticipatory bail is granted;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iv) The character, behaviour, means, position and standing of the accused;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(v) Whether accusation has been </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">made only with the object of injuring</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> or humiliating the applicant by arresting him. Because it is to be remembered that a worst agony, humiliation and disgrace is attached to arrest. Arrest leads to many consequences not only for the accused but for his entire family and at the same time for the entire community;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(vi) A balance has to be struck between two factors, namely, no </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">prejudice should be caused to free,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> fair and thorough investigation and there should be prevention of harassment, humiliation and unjustified detention of the accused;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(vii) The anticipatory bail being <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">an extra ordinary privilege, </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">should </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">be granted only in exceptional</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;"> cases.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Such extraordinary judicial discretion conferred upon the Higher Court has to be properly </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">exercised after proper application</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of mind to decide whether it is a fit case for granting anticipatory bail not according to whim, caprice or fancy;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">(viii) A condition must be imposed</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> that the applicant shall not make any inducement or threat to the witnesses for tampering the evidence of the occurrence;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(ix) The apprehension that the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">accused is in a position to influence,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> induce or coerce witnesses to desist from furnishing relevant information to the investigating agency cannot be considered to be imaginary and the court ought to have considered that aspect seriously before granting anticipatory bail.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(x) In the cases involve grave offence like murder, dacoity, robbery, rape etc. where it is necessary to arrest the accused and bring his movements under restraint to infuse confidence </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">among the terror-stricken victims</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> the accused should never be enlarged on anticipatory bail. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Such discretion should be exercised</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> with care and circumspection depending upon the facts and circumstances justifying its exercise. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xi) It is to be borne in mind about the legislative intention for </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">the purpose of granting anticipatory</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">bail because legislature has omitted</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> the provision of Section 497A from the Code.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xii) It would be improper exercise of such extraordinary judicial discretion if an accused is enlarged on anticipatory for a indefinite period which may cause interruption on the way of holding thorough and smooth investigation of the offence committed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xiii) The Court must be extremely cautious since such bail to some extent intrudes in the sphere of investigation of crime.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xiv) While enlarging an accused on anticipatory bail, the Court must direct the applicant to co-operate with the investigating officer in every steps of holding proper investigation if the same is needed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xv) The anticipatory bail granted by the Court should ordinary be continued not more than 8(eight) weeks and shall not continue after submission of charge sheet, and the same must </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">be in connection with non-bailable</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> offence.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(xvi) The Court granting anticipatory bail will be at liberty to cancel the bail if a case for cancellation of bail is otherwise made out by the State or complainant. . . . (51)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.7pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Nandini Satpathy Vs. P. L. Dani (AIR 1978 (SC) 1025); Crown Vs. Khushi Muhammad, V DLR (FC) page 86; Sadiq Ali Vs. State, [18 DLR (SC) 28]; Md. Ayub Vs. Md. Yaqub and another 19 DLR (SC)38; Golam Sarwar Kamal Vs. The State, 1986 BLD (AD) 110; Immam and others Vs. The State, 46 DLR (HCD) page 315; State Vs. M.A. Maleque, 47 DLR (AD) 33; Atiquallah Khan Masud Vs. The State, 15 BLD (AD) page 14; State Vs. Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury 51 DLR (AD) page 42; State Vs. Jakaria Pintu 62 DLR (AD) page 420; State Vs. A. Haque 15 MLR (AD)151; State Vs. Md. State (NCT of Delhi) 2018 SCC (online) 531 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>Forthe Petitioner</b>,</span><span style='font-size:8.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>(In all the cases)</span><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">: Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Attorney General (with Mr. Murad Reza, Additional Attorney General, Mr. Mamtajuddin Fakir, Additional Attorney General, Mr. Biswajith Debnath, D.A.G.), instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>Forthe Respondent</b>,</span><span style='font-size:8.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>(In Crl. Ali Azam, Advocate-on-Record. </span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 41.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes;"><td style="width: 105.4pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondent</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 7.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In Crl. P. Nos. 1203/18, 1208/18, 1209/18, 1210/18, 1211-1215/18, 1216/18, 1223/18, 1225/18, 1253/18 and 378/19)</span></p></td><td style="width: 74.85pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="100"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">: Not represented</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"> </p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 41.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes;"><td style="width: 105.4pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondent</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 8.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In Crl. P. Nos. 1203/18, 1208/18, 1209/18, 1210/18, 1211-1215/18, 1216/18, 1223/18, 1225/18, 1253/18 and 378/19)</span></p></td><td style="width: 74.85pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="100"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Khondker Mahbub </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Hossain, Senior Advocate,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> with </span></p></td></tr><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 1; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td colspan="2" style="width: 180.25pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="240"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 30.6pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Moudud Ahmed, Senior Advocate, Mr. Zainul Abedin, Senior Advocate, Mr. A.M. Mahbub Uddin, Advocate, Mr. Ruhul Quddus, Advocate, Mr. Md. Sagir Hossain Leon, Advocate, instructed by Mr. Md. Zahirul Islam, Advocate-on- Record</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>Forthe Respondent</b>,</span><span style='font-size:8.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>(In Crl. P. No.1254/18)</span><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">: Mr. Khondker Mahbub Hossain, Senior Advocate, with Mr. Moudud Ahmed, Senior Advocate, Mr. Zainul Abedin, Senior Advocate, Mr. A.M. Mahbub Uddin, Advocate, Mr. Ruhul Quddus, Advocate, Mr. Md. Sagir Hossain Leon, Advocate, instructed by Mr. Sataya Ranjan Mondal, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The question raised in all these leave petitions is whether order of granting anticipatory bail should be for a limited period or not.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">These petitions involved issue of great public importance pertaining to the importance of individual personal liberty and greater interest of the society at large. Society has a vital interest in granting anticipatory bail or refusal of the same because every criminal offence is an offence against the State.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The horizon of human rights is expanding all over the world, at the same time, crime rate is also increasing. Of late, this Court has been receiving repeated complaints about the violation of human rights because of indiscriminate arrest by the police. We need to strike the right balance between the two. The order of granting or refusing of anticipatory bail must reflect perfect balance between the two conflicting interests, namely, sanctity of individual liberty and the interest of the informant and society. Therefore, realistic approach must be made in this regard. In the case of Nandini Satpathy -Vs.- P.L. Dani (AIR 1978 (SC) 1025), it was observed by the Supreme Court of India that – </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“ To strike the balance between the needs of law of enforcement on the one hand and the protection of citizen from the oppression and injustice at the hands of law enforcement machinery on the other hand is a perennial problem of statecraft. The pendulum over the years has swung to the right”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Historical perspective as to provision of anticipatory bail</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">.</span></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, at its initiation had no specific provision of anticipatory bail. In 1978, by the Law Reforms Ordinance provision was incorporated for direction to grant of bail to person apprehending arrest, by inserting Section 497A in the Code of Criminal Procedure. The said section reads as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">“497A. Direction for grant of bail to person apprehending arrest-(1) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">When any person has reason to believe that he may be arrested on an accusation of having committed a non-bailable offence, he may apply to the High Court Division or the Court of Session or the Subdivisional Magistrate for a direction under this section; and that Court or the Magistrate may, if it or he thinks fit, direct that in the event of such arrest, he shall be released on bail. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(2) When the High Court Division or the Court of Session or the Sub-divisional Magistrate makes or gives a direction under sub- section (1), it or he may include such conditions in such directions in the light of the facts of the particular case, as it or he may think fit. (3) If such person is thereafter arrested without warrant by an officer in charge of a police station on such accusation, and is prepared either at the time of arrest or at any time while in the custody of such officer to give bail, he shall be released on bail; and if a Magistrate taking cognizance of such offence decides that a warrant should issue in the first instance against that person, he shall issue a bailable warrant in conformity with the direction of the Court or the Subdivisional Magistrate under sub-section (1)”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Thereafter, the said provision was omitted from the Code by the Code of Criminal Procedure (Amendment) Ordinance, 1982 (Ordinance No.IX of 1982). Relevant provision of the said Ordinance runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“2. Omission of section 497A, Act, V of 1978; In the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 (Act V of 1898), herein referred to as the said Code section 497A shall be omitted.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">After omission of Section 497A from the Code of Criminal Procedure, the legislature did not take any step to reintroduce any such provision in the Code of Criminal Procedure, that is, at present there is no specific law in the Code of Criminal Procedure or in any other law for granting anticipatory bail. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Jurisprudence build up in respect of granting anticipatory bail in different leading cases in our apex Court:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 24pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of [Crown Vs. Khushi Muhammad reported V DLR (FC) page 86] respondent Khusi Mohammad made a prayer before the Sessions Judge for releasing him on bail in pending investigation. The Sessions Judge rejected the prayer for bail. Then he went to the High Court, Kayani,J. made the following order: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“ I would accept this petition and direct that if it is intended to arrest him he should be released by the District Magistrate if a bail bond is furnished to his satisfaction”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Against the said decision, the petition for special leave to appeal was filed before the Federal Court. Full Bench of Federal Court granted leave to consider the question, “whether the High Court can grant any relief, and if so, to a person seeking an order of bail, in anticipation of his arrest for a offence?”. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">While setting aside the order of bail passed by Kayani, J. Abdul Rashid C.J. observed:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“After a careful examination of the provisions of section 496 and 497 and 498 of the Code, I have reached the conclusion that person cannot be admitted to bail against whom a report has been lodged at the police station but who has not been placed in custody, or under any other form of restraint, or against whom no warrant for arrest, has been issued. In the case of a person who is not under arrest, but for whose arrest warrants have been issued, bail can be granted under Section 498 if he appears in Court and surrender himself.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of Sadiq Ali Vs. State, [18 DLR (SC) 28], the appellant Sadiq Ali made an application before the Sessions Judge for anticipatory bail and the learned Sessions Judge granted him ad-interim bail and issued notice to the Public Prosecutor. On the date fixed the appellant and Public Prosecutor were heard and finally, the application for bail was rejected and appellant Sadiq Ali was ordered that he be remanded to Police custody but he escaped from that custody. He moved a petition in the High Court Division, the High Court Division directed him to appear before the Subordinate Judge but in the meantime, the police had sent up chargesheet against him. Ad-interim order was extended till that date. The mater went before the Supreme Court to resolve the question of general importance affecting the power of Criminal Courts to grant bail before arrest. S.A. Rahman, J. finally observed in the case of Sadiq Ali as under: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“It seems there is no decided case in England in which anticipatory bail might have been allowed to an accused person, threatened with arrest by the police. The practice of the English Courts, however, cannot be decisive of the point that confronts us in this case and which calls for decision on interpretation of the language of our own written Codes, in the light of conditions prevailing in this country. Of course, even in the case of an imminent police arrest, no order should be passed for grant of bail by a Court, unless the petitioner personally appears before the Court, even under Pakistan law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">As a result of the above discussion, I have reached the conclusion that the rule laid down in Khushi Muhammad's case could be safely extended to a direction for the grant of bail to a person, whose arrest, on a criminal charge by the police, without a warrant, is proved to be imminent and certain, and where the circumstances would justify the grant of bail. Such an interpretation, in my humble judgment, is consistent with the language of sections 496 and 497 of the Code and involves no widening of the scope of the power given by section 498 as compared with its extent under the former sections. Indeed, such an order might be eminently called for, in certain circumstances of grave character, affecting the liberty of a citizen. Indiscriminate grant of bail, however, merely on the request of a person, who appears in Court, and thereby surrenders himself to that Court, without the other conditions for such bail being satisfied, would amount to an act of judicial extravagance which cannot be countenanced.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Next case is the case of Md. Ayub Vs. Md. Yaqub and another reported in 19 DLR (SC)38. In that case, respondent Md. Yaqub moved a petition for bail in the High Court which was dismissed. Thereafter, he filed another petition before another Judge and obtained bail. The complainant went to the Supreme Court. Five members of Bench of the Supreme Court heard the matter. S.A. Rahman J., observed in that case: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“I have come to the conclusion that the view in Sadiq Ali case may require a little modification in so far as the word “appears” in section 496 and 497, need not be construed to include voluntary appearance, even in circumstances of grave apprehension of arrest. This more may be taken to have been used in sections 496 and 497, in the same sense as in section 242 or 252 of the Code, which obviously contemplate appearance in answer to a process issued by a Court.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Fazle Akbar, J. agreed with the judgment delivered by S.A. Rahman, J. While agreeing with the judgment delivered by S.A. Rahman, J. C.J. Cornelius observed:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“I consider that, on recognised principles of statutory construction, the effect of section 498, can be reconciled with that of section 497, without doing violence to the meaning of any expression used in either section, and at the same time, with complete adequacy, on the reasoning set out in the judgment of my learned brother, S.A. Rahman, J.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Hamoodur Rahman, J. made his observation with following language:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Taking into account the context in which section 498 appears and the wide words deliberately used in it in respect of the power of granting bail it seems to me that it is in the nature of a residuary and supplementary provision giving to superior criminal Courts, namely, the High Court and the Court of Session, a wider power to grant bail in appropriate cases, to persons to whom bail cannot be granted under sections 496 and 497. In what manner this power should be exercised or what principles these superior Courts should be guided in exercising their discretion is an altogether different question and should not, in my view , be taken into account for determining the true scope of this section. In my view, there can be no doubt that section 498 gives extended and wider powers to the High Court and the Court of Sessions but this power will no doubt normally be exercised in a reasonable and judicial manner taking into account the limitations placed by other provisions of the Code upon subordinate authorities and that a rule founded on justice and equity will not be disregarded unless there be exceptional circumstances. But this is a self imposed restriction and not a restriction imposed by anything contained in the section. Normally this general salutary principle will no doubt be kept in view and will not be lightly departed from but this should not, in my view, be held to debar the High Court and the Court of Session from deviating from it in exceptional cases or a controlling the wide words of section 498 as a matter construction of the section. This principle is invoked in aid more as a precaution against the indiscriminate grant of bail and not as a statutory Prolog upon the powers of these Courts.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">On the other hand, Muhammad Yaqub Ali, J. made observation with the following words:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“The words “in any case” do away with <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the distinction made in section 497 between</span> cases punishable with transportation for life and death and cases involving lesser penalty. Similarly the use of the words “any person” confer jurisdiction in respect of person who may not be under arrest and does not appear in obedience to the process issued by the Court or are not brought before the Court as envisaged in Section 497. It is the effect of these words which, in my opinion, justify grant of bail before arrest and not the subtle difference between the words “release on bail” and “admit to bail” used in section 497 and 498 respectively.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of Golam Sarwar Kamal Vs. The State, reported in 1986 BLD (AD) 110 while granting anticipatory bail, this Division observed as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“From the facts stated in the petition and the circumstances mentioned therein, it appears that the appellant may reasonably apprehend that the police might arrest him to prevent his participation in the election.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, bail was granted to the appellant by this Court on 28-1-84 till one week after holding of the postponed election.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of Jahanara Immam and others Vs. The State, reported in 46 DLR (HCD) page 315, the High Court admitted the petitioners on bail and directed the Metropolitan Magistrate to pass an order immediately admitting them to bail after their surrender within 3(three) weeks from the date of his order.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The next case is the case of State Vs. M.A. Maleque, reported in 47 DLR(AD)33. In that case, the High Court Division directed the respondent M.A. Maleque to surrender before the concerned Court within 14(fourteen) days. Against which, the State filed criminal petition in the Appellate Division. While disposing of the petition, the Appellate Division, considering the special facts of the case, observed that it was difficult to hold that High Court exercise its decision unreasonably and unfairly.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of Atiquallah Khan Masud Vs. The State, reported in 15BLD(AD) page 14 the High Court Division rejected the prayer for anticipatory bail. Atikullah Khan Masud came to the Appellate Division. This Division in the said case observed that unquestionably, the High Court Division has power under Section 498 of the Code of Criminal Procedure to grant bail to the appellant. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Important case in this regard is in the case of State Vs. Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury reported 51 DLR (AD) page 42. Five members Bench of this Division (main judgment was written by A.T.M. Afzal, C.J.) taking into consideration of the above mentioned decisions observed that in our country, it has almost become customary by practice through decades to approach the higher Court straight way if there was a prayer for anticipatory bail which was very rare. Apart from practice we consider it appropriate and desirable that the remedy being extra-ordinary such matters should be considered at the level of the High Court Division. It was further observed: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Now we come to the real point at issue as to the conditions and circumstances under which an application for pre-arrest or anticipatory bail can be considered under section 498 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. We wish to lay down as a first proposition that <u>it is an extraordinary remedy, and an exception to the general law of bail which can be granted only in extraordinary and exceptional circumstances upon a proper and intelligent exercise of discretion.”</u> (underlined by us).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Generally speaking the main circumstances as would entitle an order for extra-ordinary remedy of pre arrest bail is the perception of the Court upon the facts and materials disclosed by the petitioner before it that the Criminal proceeding which is being or has been launched against him is being or has been taken with an ulterior motive, political or otherwise , for harassing the accused and not for securing justice, in a particular case”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">In cited case Latifur Rahman, J. wrote separate judgment with the following observation:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Anticipatory bail should be granted by the High Court Division for a limited period or till filing of the charge-sheet whichever is appropriate in the circumstances of the case. After expiry of the period or filing of the charge-sheet, as the case may be, the accused must appear before the Court concerned and obtain fresh bail from the Court on the merit of the case.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Finally, it was observed:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Before parting with the cases, I feel that since there is a Law Commission in Bangladesh the matter may be referred by the Government before the Law Commission for incorporating a section in the Code of Criminal Procedure for granting anticipatory bail as has been done by the Law Commission of India by inserting section 438 in the Indian Criminal Procedure Code. By such legislation there will be a specific statutory sanction of granting anticipatory bail with positive conditions and directions.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We are not informed as to whether the Law Commission has taken any such step in the light of observation made above till today. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of State Vs. Jakaria Pintu reported in 62 DLR (AD) page 420 6(six) members bench of this Division (judgment was delivered by A.B.M. Khairul Haque, J) has observed –</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Let me now consider the impugned order. With great respect, the order passed by the learned Judges gives an impression that they did not even go through the first information report in considering the petition for bail. The order does not reflect it at all. It does not state a word about the incident which resulted the death of a human being but granted bail, an anticipatory one, to the main accused on invoking the Constitutional right of the accused. But it was the first legal duty of the accused persons to surrender either before the police or before the concerned Magistrate before invoking their Constitutional right, although we are not aware of their any other right but the obligation to surrender as above. After all, the victims also have their various rights under the same very Constitution.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“This petition also gives me an opportunity to remind all concerned which is sometimes forgotten that a bail although may often be right to an accused but sometimes it is imperative on the part of the Court to refuse if there is serious allegations against him, like murder, rape, violence etc., because the Court must always keep in mind that justice must ultimately be done by ensuring punishment upon the offender, otherwise, the offenders will get upper hand and the sober section of the society will suffer, which will destroy the fabrics of the civilised society.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of State Vs. A. Haque reported in 15 MLR (AD)151 this Division discouraged in granting anticipatory bail indiscriminately holding that the High Court Division will be slow in granting consequential relief under Section 498 on an application for anticipatory bail.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The next case is the case of the State Vs. Md. Monirul Islam @ Nirob and others reported in 16 BLC (AD) page 53. (judgment was delivered by A.B.M. Khairul Haque, C.J.) In that case it was observed,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“We have gone through the Order dated 08.06.2010 passed by the learned Judges of the High Court Division. The Order granting the ad interim anticipatory bail is absolutely mechanical and does not give any reason for giving such an exceptional relief. This kind of blanket order allowing anticipatory bail should not be passed. True it is, that it is an ad interim bail but it is still a bail. As such, the learned judges ought to be satisfied before allowing anticipatory bail, ad interim or otherwise as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">i) The allegation is vague,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">ii) No material is on record to substantiate the allegations,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">iii) There is no reasonable apprehension that the witnesses may be tampered with,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">iv)The apprehension of the applicant that he will be unnecessarily harassed, appears to be justified before the Court, on the materials on record,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">v) Must satisfy the criteria for granting bail under section 497 of the Code,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">vi) The allegations are made for collateral purpose but not for securing justice for the victim.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">vii) There is a compelling circumstance for granting such bail,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In this connection, we should all remember that the power to grant bail, an anticipatory one, should not be exercised arbitrarily. This is an extraordinary relief and should be granted judiciously and sparingly only in an exceptional circumstances as stated above and not otherwise. The status of the applicant or his high station of life, affluence is not at all relevant in considering the application for anticipatory bail. But if there is apprehension that granting of bail may impede public interest such as security of the State or hamper investigation by the police, the application for bail should be refused. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>Since power of the Court to grant anticipatory bail was allowed by insertion of section 497A which was again promptly repealed within a very short-time, the indication is clear, showing legislative apathy towards granting of such bail. In these days, no body seems to remember the sad plight of the victims and their relations. We must remember and appreciate that they are also equally seeker of even handed justice. A Judge should never be oblivion <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">of their sufferings, indignity and harassment whenever he considers the question of bail, anticipatory or otherwise. He must always remember that the administration of justice is the ultimate aim whenever he passes any order.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In dealing with an application for bail the Judge must also remember that the course of investigation should never be impeded, otherwise, the course of justice may be frustrated. That cannot be allowed. The Judge must also remember that the purpose of allowing an anticipatory bail is to give the applicant a temporary respite in a proceeding which <span style="letter-spacing: -.1pt;">is apparently commenced not for securing justice but for some collateral purpose. But ultimately he has to appear before the concerned Court of the Magistrate. <strong><u>As such, in proper cases anticipatory bail may be granted but for a very short period, such as between 2 to 4 weeks and not for a long period of time.</u> </strong>( underlined by us). It must also be remembered that sooner he appears before the Magistrate the better. The Magistrate after hearing both the parties would do the needful. If any of the parties is aggrieved, he may always seek justice in a higher forum. But such a bail should not be for a longer period which may impede the investigation.”</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">That is, in this case it has been specifically stated that anticipatory bail may be granted for a very short period. It is more specifically mentioned that the same may be for a period from 2 to 4 weeks.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Thereafter, this Division in the case of Durnity Daman Commission and another Vs. Dr. Khandaker Mosharraf Hossain and another <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">reported in 66 DLR (AD) 92 (judgment was delivered by A.H.M. Shamsuddin Choudhury.J)</span> has observed as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“A metaphorical avowal that the Magistracy/lower judiciary is controlled by the executive should not be treated as specific because Magistrates/lower court/ tribunal Judges do no longer dwel in the realm governed by the executive. If allegation of bias is aired against a particular or a group of Magistrates/ Judges, cause of suspicion must be specifically spelt out. The Judges concerned, shall give reasons for their satisfaction on this unraveling point </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(b) Political threshold of the petitioner or claimed rivalry, by itself, without further ado, shall not be a ground for entertaining an application. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(c)Non-bailability of the offence cited in the FIR cannot be a reason for the High Court Division’s intervention for even the Magistrates/lower court/tribunal Judges are competent enough to enlarge on bail a person accused of non-bailable offences in deserving cases. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(d)Effect of the accused’s freedom on the investigation process must not be allowed to float on obfuscation. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(f) The High Court Division must scrutinize the text in the FIR with expected diligence and shall ordinarily be indisposed to grant anticipatory bail where the allegations are of heinous nature, keeping in mind the ordains figured at paragraph 19 of the case reported in 51DLR(AD), 242. Claim that the allegations are cooked up shall also not be adjudged at that of point if the FIR or the complaint petition, as the case is, prima facie, discloses an offence. Whether the allegations are framed or genuine can only be determined through investigation and sifting of evidence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(g) Interest of the victim in particular and the society at large must be taken into account in weighing respective rights. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(h) <u>If satisfied in all respect, the High Court Division shall dispose of the application instantaneously by enlarging the accused a limited bail, not normally exceeding four weeks, without issuing any Rule.</u> It must be conspicuously stated in the bail granting order that in the event of any filance of bail application, the Court below will consider the same using its own legal discretion without reference to the High Court Division’s anticipatory bail order. Anticipatory bails shall not survive post charge-sheet stage.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of State Vs.
